Sinclair Lewis's Masterpiece "Main Street" Translated and Published

Sinclair Lewis, the American novelist who won the 1930 Nobel Prize in Literature, wrote the masterpiece "Main Street," a new realistic work and one of the masterpieces of European and American novels of this century, satirizing the forces of mediocrity in society and resonating with social struggles. The author spent a long time carefully writing it in three drafts. The original was printed in dozens of editions in the United States, with sales of over 800,000 copies, and translated into various European countries. Now, Yang Jun Zongqing (signed Bai Hua) translated it into Chinese for the first time, published in the Tianjin Guowen Weekly (from Volume 8, Issue 29 to Volume 9, Issue 14), which was quite popular among readers. Recently, this book has been published in a separate edition, divided into two volumes, about 800 pages, with a total of 300,000 words, beautifully bound and printed, with valuable photos, and published on May 10th. The price per volume is eight corners, plus postage of two corners and five cents. It is sold by the publishing department of the Tianjin Ta Kung Pao. Art-loving friends should not miss it.

Correspondence

To Those Studying in the Soviet Union for Educational Forestry (2)

(Li Yingong)

(2) Can fallen leaves and pine needles be sold as fuel, and what is the annual amount? (Answer) This is due to a complete lack of knowledge of the mountain forest life in our country. This question was raised by a member at a gathering of social educators in Zhenjiang that I attended some time ago. Because the guests were talking loudly, there was no time to interject and defend, and eventually they all dispersed. Now, it is like having a bone in my throat that I cannot help but spit out. Please tell that person that in the habits of East Asian nations where livelihoods are almost exhausted, there is indeed a way to use fallen leaves and pine needles to replace firewood (all countries that value forests retain the undergrowth as natural fertilizer, referred to as ForestFloor). This custom has not been completely eliminated to this day. However, how often have you seen a mountain owner or landlord collect and sell them in the market? Not only is this impossible, but may I ask, in the educational forest areas, which mountain grasses are not open to the villagers without conditions every year from September to October, allowing them to pick them up without taking a penny? Even this is not easy to win the favor of the villagers around the forest. Even in areas such as Jiangnan Tangshan Second Forest Farm, it is necessary to open it twice a year. In the Xiaojiuhua District of the Central Model Forest, because of refusing this custom, it evolved into a disturbance that destroyed the district office and injured the police. If all mountain forest products were valued and priced like in the city, then the income of the by-products in the district I was inspecting would not have amounted to only 16,840 yuan and 43 cents. In my opinion, it was the result of exhausting my efforts and increasing it year by year. Some people in the Soviet Union may despise it as insignificant. Could it be that there is a preconceived notion of distrusting people from other provinces in their minds?

(3) Although the trees have not yet reached maturity, why can't a portion be harvested and sold to provide funds for use? (Answer) Any measures that do not conform to the principles of forest management can be corrected by passersby. Now, how can there be any value in discussing proposals that violate the laws of nature? The circumference of young tree stems is narrow, unlike the trunks of middle-aged and older trees, which can be several feet in circumference. Therefore, the volume of a measured year ring can exceed ten times and is not yet complete. Therefore, a forestry enterprise must be wealthy and patient to wait until the highest rate of growth before harvesting. (Note that each tree species has its highest rate of growth in a year, and beyond this, it gradually decreases, like a Curueline of market prices in economics. This situation varies depending on climate and soil, and depending on seeds, so it needs to be tested before it can be said with certainty.) Moreover, the growth rate of single and upright trees is far less than that of forest trees, which cannot be expected to be understood by everyone. Now, the property values of each educational forest area have long been recorded in tree surveys, sampling diagrams of the material growth of major tree species, and zoning forest maps. Therefore, the operations are as clear as the palm of one's hand, and there are designated areas for testing new methods, such as direct sowing, from broadleaf to coniferous trees, cluster afforestation methods, tending methods without pruning, grafting methods, cutting experiments, adaptation experiments for mixed forests, and the trial planting of more than ninety new tree species from Sichuan and Kang… etc. In terms of age, the largest forests have just reached their peak. How can one suddenly expect them to be produced and sold, which is like expecting a three-foot-tall child to be a pillar of the family? It is difficult to do so. In general, the proper way to cultivate a forest is to introduce a source of benefits that lasts for a long time. If this can be done, then farmland will be directly and indirectly affected and avoid crop failure. The hundred industries of the surrounding villages can also rely on it to flourish day by day. In the past, the manager of the Chongyalou Forest Garden in Wuning, Jiangxi, the supervisor of the Linmu Farm in Yixing Huxiazhen, the representative of the Fulou Company in Tianwang Temple, Jurong, and the owner of the Jiufeng Forest Farm in Xishan, Beiping, all came to inquire, and I told them all the same purpose in writing, and I was happy to do my best to advise those who were engaged in this industry.

Local News

Exports to the United States in the First Three Months

The Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury reported that, according to the announcement of the US Consulate General, the total value of Chinese goods shipped to the United States in the first three months of this year, of which those requiring customs declarations, was US$8,837,568. The value of gold bars exported to the United States was US$5,629,031. For the month of March alone, the export to the United States was US$3,509,050 for goods and US$3,583,884 for gold bars. Furthermore, the total value of goods shipped to the United States from Shanghai in the first four months of this year was US$5,905,048.

National Goods Promotion Association Holds Meeting Today

Regarding the goods stored at the Zhabei National Exhibition

The Shanghai Citizens National Goods Promotion Association led various factories to hold the Zhabei National Exhibition on January 15. Affected by the invasion of the brutal Japanese army, it was suspended midway, and all the goods were stored in the Yuyetang, heavily locked and carefully arranged. On February 15, the Citizens General Association allocated a fake ambulance to transport the goods, accompanied by the transportation committee, risking danger. Unexpectedly, the locks were broken and the doors were broken, and the scene was a mess. The remaining goods were temporarily packed and transported by car one after another and returned to each factory. Due to time constraints, they could not be transported completely. Later, after the National Army withdrew, there was no opportunity to transport them again, and it has been delayed until now, resulting in heavy losses. Yesterday, a letter was received from Mr. Wang Binyan, stating that at night, thugs armed with weapons attempted to rob the machines and other items deposited by the association. The resident group members resisted and thwarted their plan. Since they have been coveted, it is extremely difficult to prevent them. It is heard that police power will be restored in the near future. As soon as transportation is convenient, please write back to discuss ways to transport the goods, etc. The association believes that it is in the interests of each factory and should immediately plan for protection. It is specially scheduled to convene executive and supervisory committee members and members of the National Exhibition at the association's office at Jiumudi at 3:00 PM today (19th) to discuss proper measures to facilitate transportation.

Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces

Subsidy Fees Issued for Silk Exports Yesterday

Entrusted to the China and Four Other Banks

Customs Ordered to Stop Collecting Silk Export Tax

To rescue the silk and cocoon industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, after the government appointed special commissioners and established the Committee for the Reorganization of Obsolete Silks and Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang and the Committee for the Promotion of Obsolete Silks in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, they immediately engaged in registration. The Jianghai Customs in this city also received orders to stop collecting export taxes on raw silk and surcharges on the Silk Industry Public Bonds Fund from yesterday. At the same time, the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces implemented the issuance of export subsidies for raw silk. The details of each item are recorded as follows:

Announcement to Stop Collection

Tang Hai'an, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Mei Lehe, Customs Commissioner, received orders from the Ministry of Finance to stop collecting the export tax on white silk, spun silk, yellow silk, douyan silk, and waste silk listed in Articles 180 to 184 of the Export Tariff, and the original special donation (i.e., the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bonds Fund Surcharge) from May 18. They immediately complied with the order and implemented it, and announced it to the public on the same day.

Issuance of Subsidies

A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency visited Mr. Shen Huachen, a member of the Committee for the Reorganization of Obsolete Silks and Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, yesterday. According to him, for every dan of raw silk spun from obsolete silks and cocoons in the factories of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces that have been registered with the committee, the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang will grant a subsidy of 100 taels of silver when they are transported and sold overseas. The China, Communications, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Local four banks have now been entrusted to handle the matter. The procedures for issuing subsidy vouchers are based on the inspection bureau's public weight list and the raw silk export certificate issued by the Jianghai Customs to the export merchants, starting from the date when the Jianghai Customs stopped collecting silk export taxes as announced by the Ministry of Finance. However, products from outside the two provinces and silk, yellow silk, yellow cocoons, dougong silk, cocoon pillows for domestic use are not eligible for subsidies. The government has now allocated 2.2 million taels for subsidies.

Public Notice to All Sectors

The Committee for the Reorganization of Obsolete Silks and Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang announced yesterday that the procedures for registration have been notified in succession. The key points that should be noted are specially notified as follows: (1) The registration date for other places is limited to May 20 and will not be extended. (2) If the registered obsolete silks and cocoons from Jiangsu and Zhejiang need to be transferred to another warehouse or transferred to another household, a written report must be submitted to the committee, indicating the number of packages, the name of the warehouse, and the warehouse receipt number for re-registration in the general registration book. (3) If the registered obsolete cocoons are to be shipped out of the warehouse and transported to a factory for silk reeling, a written report must be submitted to the committee in advance, indicating the warehouse receipt number of a certain warehouse and the number of packages to be shipped to which factory. (4) When the committee sends personnel to inspect the warehouses where the registered obsolete cocoons are stored, the method is to take out several packages from each batch of cocoons to weigh and calculate the weight, and to take a small sample of one pound from each batch of cocoons. Please provide convenience and assistance to the warehouse for handling. (5) All registered (A) obsolete silk and cocoons from other places, (B) obsolete silk from obsolete cocoons and cocoons in warehouses in this and other places must be transferred to the Shanghai Silk and Cocoon Warehouse for inspection. This is a special notice. I hope you will pay attention to it.

New Cocoons on the Market

In Shengxian, Shaoxing, Xiaoshan, Yuyao, Huzhou, Hangzhou, Haining, and other places in Zhejiang Province, the new cocoons have already been put on the market, and the cocoon merchants are handling the purchases according to the announcements and regulations of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. The highest price for Dutch varieties is 25 yuan per dan, and the highest price for improved varieties is 35 yuan per dan. Due to weather damage, the number of new cocoons harvested is even less than in previous years, and the number of households raising silkworms has been greatly reduced, which has greatly affected the economy of the farmers. It is expected that the new cocoons in Jiaxing and Pinghu in Zhejiang Province will be put on the market within a few days. However, the new cocoons in Wuxi, Liyang, Changzhou, and other places in Jiangsu Province will have to wait until the end of this month.

Wuzhen Road Bridge and Mongolia Road Intersection

Reopening Today to Restore Traffic

After the outbreak of the Shanghai war, Zhabei and other places were used as battlefields, and barbed wire fences and sandbags were placed at the junctions of the Chinese and Foreign Concessions, cutting off traffic. After the signing of the armistice agreement, the Japanese army subsequently withdrew. The Japanese army in the fourth district of the Public Security Bureau south of the railway also withdrew a few days ago, and our police took over. The city's commerce has gradually recovered. In addition to the Hengfeng Road Bridge in the area, which has been unblocked earlier, the Wuzhen Road Bridge, Xinzhaji, and Mongolia Road intersection (as for the changes), have not yet been restored. The municipal authorities have requested the Municipal Council to find a way to open the above-mentioned main roads. According to Huang Ming, the captain of the brigade and director of the Shanghai North Office, who spoke to a reporter from the Guowen News Agency yesterday, except for the Xinzhaji Bridge, the Wuzhen Road Bridge and Mongolia Road intersection have been approved by the Municipal Council to be opened from tomorrow morning (8th) to restore traffic.

Interview with Members of the Postal Workers Unions

Report on the Truth about the Postal Foundation Consolidation Plan

The Shanghai Postal Workers Union and the Employees Union submitted a plan to the Ministry of Communications to consolidate the postal foundation. To clarify the situation, reporters specially visited Qi Jiamou, a standing committee member of the Postal Workers Union, yesterday. The following is a record of the interview: (Reporter) Your association's plan has many items. What is the main purpose? (Answer) Our association believes that the post office has fallen into a state of deficit. Therefore, we want to seek a fundamental remedy. We have specially put forward a concrete plan. The main method is to merge the Savings and Remittance Bureau and implement special postal accounting to maintain the good Li postal system and consolidate the economic foundation. (Question) The Savings and Remittance Bureau has been separated for three years. Why do you insist on merging it now? (Answer) Before the Savings and Remittance Bureau was created, both our associations and the postal workers across the country first opposed it. In the years 18 and 19, we submitted documents to the Ministry of Communications requesting a merger. Even at the beginning of Minister Chen's appointment last year, we sent representatives to prepare documents requesting a merger. In the past, our association remained quiet and observed how the bureau was operating. To maintain the post office, we did not take active action. However, the separate establishment of the bureau has caused the post office to suffer losses. Therefore, our association should not delay any longer at this time and ask for a merger. In short, merging the Savings and Remittance Bureau is the only way to save the post office. The claim does not start from today. (Question) The merger of the Savings and Remittance Bureau is easily misunderstood as a personnel issue. How do you explain it? (Answer) Our association resolutely advocated the merger of the Savings and Remittance Bureau during the tenure of Wang Boqun, the former Minister of Communications. Our association's past movements have all been to safeguard national undertakings and the interests of the people, and to seek the integrity of power. There are absolutely no other issues. Just look at our association's bright history, and the outside world's misunderstandings will naturally be dispelled, etc.

General Labor Union

Telegram to Request Adoption of Postal Workers' Suggestions

Yesterday, the Shanghai General Labor Union sent a telegram to the Ministry of Transportation, stating: "To Minister of Transportation Chen Jun: It is our humble opinion that the Chinese postal system has achieved remarkable results and annual surpluses due to its well-structured system and meticulous management over the years. However, since the recovery of postal rights, the postal system has been subject to the control of political tides, losing its independence. Furthermore, with unqualified personnel in charge, national public utilities are being used to serve private interests. This has led to the establishment of superfluous organizations, shaking the foundation of the postal system, increasing expenditures, and wasting postal funds, resulting in the current situation of deficits. Tracing the root cause, this is a dangerous start. Now, they are attempting to compensate by increasing postal rates, which is like drinking poison to quench thirst, and can hardly be considered a good plan. In recent years, China's internal affairs have not been well managed, and there has been no construction. State-owned enterprises, apart from the postal system, such as railways, telecommunications, and aviation, have accumulated numerous malpractices and suffered huge losses. However, since the recovery of postal rights, even the last remaining achievement of the postal system has been ruined to this extent, inviting ridicule from foreign guests and jeopardizing the nation's lifeline, which is extremely disheartening. The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Postal Staff Union, based on their years of observation, have submitted a concrete plan to your ministry to consolidate the foundation of the postal system. The measures proposed, such as abolishing the Savings and Remittance General Bureau, ceasing aviation subsidies, ensuring the economic viability of the postal system, and using postal revenue to support the postal system, reflect deep thought, foresight, and a thorough understanding of the root causes, and are truly fundamental measures to consolidate the foundation of the postal system. We humbly request that your ministry promptly adopt and implement these measures, and revoke the order to increase postal rates, so as not to disappoint the postal workers' ardent desire to protect the postal system, and to live up to the earnest expectations of the people. We respectfully submit this telegram, and hope for your consideration and approval." Respectfully, the Shanghai General Labor Union.

Recent News from the War Zone Refugee Relief Association

Currently Processing Repatriation

Subsequent Suspension of Shelter

The Shanghai area, with its bustling commercial districts and dense population, has been reduced to ruins since the January 28th Incident this year. Residents and merchants have been displaced and suffered greatly. The number of victims is countless. Charitable and public welfare organizations in Shanghai immediately established a temporary war zone refugee relief association to provide rescue and shelter with utmost effort. It is reported that the number of shelters has increased to thirty-one, and there are four hospitals. More than 300,000 refugees have been rescued so far. Now that the ceasefire has been implemented, the association has issued a notice, which is recorded below: "It is hereby notified that the war in Shanghai has ceased. The temporary shelters and hospitals established by the association are now being closed down and refugees are being repatriated. All shelters will be absolutely suspended from accepting new refugees."

News of French Mail Ship Fire Yesterday

Fifty-One Chinese Sailors Rescued

Mail on Board Completely Burned

The French Mail Ship Company's new vessel, the Georges Philippar, caught fire in the Red Sea, causing damage to the entire ship and losses of 20 million yuan. Many passengers and crew members were killed or injured. Further news from yesterday is summarized below:

Passengers Flee in Panic

A Reuters dispatch from Aden on the 17th reported that passengers rescued from the French ship Georges Philippar described the circumstances of the incident, stating that the fire spread rapidly upon discovery and was impossible to extinguish. All chemical fire extinguishers and hoses on board were ineffective. The flames spread quickly through the upper-level painted walls and decorations. As the fire spread, the radio room managed to send out a distress signal before being destroyed. The alert received by distant ships was relayed by two British ships and a Russian oil tanker. When the crew awakened the passengers and urged them to evacuate quickly, the resulting chaos was indescribable. Because the bow of the ship was downwind, flames and thick smoke engulfed the stern. Many lifeboats were quickly destroyed, and passengers could not reach their assigned evacuation stations. Husbands and wives, parents and children, could not look after each other. However, there were many life preservers and rafts on board, and many passengers jumped into the calm sea and were rescued by other ships. Among those rescued, some suffered burns, two of whom were seriously injured and sent to the hospital for treatment after landing. Mr. and Mrs. Alford, the president of the Annam Court, were rescued, but their daughter and son-in-law are missing.

Shih Chao-chi Not on Board

A National News Agency dispatch from Paris on the 17th reported that the name of Shih Chao-chi, the former Chinese envoy to Britain, was listed on the passenger manifest of the French merchant ship Georges Philippar, which recently had an accident. However, Shih Chao-chi was not among the rescued passengers who arrived safely in Paris. After receiving this news, the Associated Press inquired about the truth in Shanghai. It was reported that the Aden report was likely inaccurate, as recent reports of Shih's whereabouts indicated that he was still traveling in Spain and Portugal and would not have been on the French ship traveling west. The French Mail Ship Company's headquarters in Paris announced today that the number of passengers was 483, bringing the total number of passengers and crew members to 740. The passenger embarkation locations were recorded as follows: Kobe (4), Shanghai (135), Saigon (265), with the remainder boarding in Singapore. However, this record is only a preliminary report of the Georges Philippar accident and should not be considered exhaustive. Furthermore, passengers rescued after the Georges Philippar accident have safely arrived in Aden on two British ships. Approximately 80 to 100 people are feared to have been burned to death on board.

Survival of Chinese Sailors

The vessel employed seventy Chinese sailors. When the ship caught fire, each of them struggled to grab life jackets and small boats to escape. Some were unable to escape and were burned to death in the fire, while others fell into the sea and were bitten by sharks and drowned. Yesterday, news from Athens reported that fifty-one of the Chinese sailors had been rescued, while nineteen were still missing. Most of them either died in the fire or drowned.

Investigation of Passenger Casualties

Yesterday, news from Athens reported that the Georges Philippar accident occurred on the afternoon of the 15th, starting with an explosion in the engine room. Because the entire ship was powered by electricity, a massive jolt was followed by simultaneous fires everywhere. The bow and stern of the ship were particularly intense. Although the ship was equipped with chemical fire extinguishers, attempts to extinguish the fire were completely ineffective. The captain immediately ordered the radio room to send out a distress signal, but the fire had already reached the radio room before the message could be completed and it was quickly destroyed. Passengers fled in panic, some grabbing lifeboats, some grabbing life jackets, and some jumping into the sea. Some of those rescued had been injured by fish bites. It has now been confirmed that dozens of people have died, and the captain and Athens branch are still being instructed to investigate further.

Shanghai Relatives Inquire

Yesterday, many relatives of passengers who boarded the ship on April 23rd to travel to France went to the French company in Shanghai to inquire about the safety of the passengers after the ship accident and whether any Chinese passengers from Shanghai had died. The company, unable to obtain detailed information, promised to send telegrams to inquire about the whereabouts of each individual.

Mr. Muirhead Rescued

Reuters, 17th

London reports that Mr. Muirhead, the British deputy inspector of the Hankou River Patrol, and his wife were passengers on the ill-fated French ship Georges Philippar. He has telegraphed his brother, saying that he and his wife were rescued by a Russian ship and are safe and sound.

Ship to Remain a Shell

The intensity of the fire on the ship is unprecedented. Since the fire started on the afternoon of the 15th, it has been burning for three days, and the fires in each cabin have not yet subsided. The cabins, furnishings, equipment, and cargo have been completely destroyed and cannot be extinguished. The Athens branch is busy rescuing passengers and can only allow the fire to continue burning. A large batch of mail from Shanghai and other places was reportedly unable to be retrieved and was completely burned.

Substantial Fire Insurance

National News Agency, London, 17th - According to Lloyd's Company today, the French ship Philippar was insured for £1.25 million, with British insurance companies underwriting half of the amount.

French Mail Company Denies Rumors

National News Agency, Paris, 17th (Night) - The French Mail Ship Company issued a statement strongly denying rumors that the Georges Philippar ship accident was due to a communist conspiracy to sink the Suez Canal and obstruct the transport of European munitions to Japan. They stated that all evidence indicates that the fire was caused by an electrical fault in the first-class cabin and that there is no evidence of a communist conspiracy.

Mrs. Valentin Talks About the Fire

National News Agency, Aden, 18th - Mrs. Valentin, the wife of the Chief Engineer of the Tianjin Kailan Mining Company, who was also on the French mail ship Georges Philippar returning to Europe, arrived safely here today after being rescued. She stated that it is certain that many passengers were buried in the fire because the fire spread very quickly, preventing many passengers from escaping from the cabins. Although the crew immediately launched lifeboats after discovering the fire, many people were already trapped inside the fire. The fire appeared to have started inside the paneling beneath the floor of the empty cabins. She first noticed an anomaly in the ceiling lights and wanted to press the call button for a waiter, but the wall switch fell off at her touch, and she felt that the electrical wire was very hot and would burn her hand. She was terrified and ran to the deck. Mrs. Valentin's words indicate that the fire on the ship was due to an electrical fault in the empty cabins. It is also reported that over a hundred people have perished in the fire.

Effective from the 20th

The Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway Transportation Department, in order to facilitate the needs of passengers, will change the schedule of the existing express and slow passenger trains, without increasing or decreasing the number of carriages. The changes will be effective from the 20th of this month. The changes will be effective from the 20th of this month. Please inform all." The timetable is recorded below. Up trains: Train 39, slow train, departs from Zhapu at 7:00 AM and arrives at Shanghai South Station at 1:53 PM; Train 35, early express, departs from Zhapu at 8:30 AM and arrives at South Station at 2:26 PM; Train 33, special express, departs from Zhapu at 2:00 PM and arrives at South Station at 6:45 PM; Zhapu-Jiading commuter train departs from Zhapu at 4:00 PM and arrives at Jiading at 7:20 PM; Jiading-Zhapu commuter train departs from Jiading at 6:05 AM and arrives at Zhapu at 9:05 AM; Jiading-Shanghai commuter train departs from Jiading at 6:30 AM and arrives at Shanghai South Station at 9:15 AM.

Jiangjing Steamer Returns to Port Due to Engine Damage

Passengers and Cargo Safe

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiangjing steamer departed from Shanghai yesterday morning around 8:00 AM, fully loaded with passengers and cargo, bound for Hankou. Around 10:00 AM, while passing near the Wenzaobang Railway Wharf, the engine steam pipe suddenly broke, causing the rudder to malfunction. The ship then anchored at that location and is currently being prepared to return to Shanghai for repairs. Fortunately, the company's Taishun steamer, arriving in Shanghai from Qingdao, approached the area. The Jiangjing's first mate immediately signaled, and after seeing the signal, the Taishun approached the ship. The shipowner then sent the first mate on the Taishun steamer to Shanghai to report to the head office. The head office then dispatched two tugboats, the Huide and Defeng, to Wenzaobang to tow the Jiangjing back to Shanghai. Around 6:00 PM, the ship was towed to Jinliyuan Wharf, and passengers disembarked one after another to transfer to other ships to continue their journey. The shipowner reported the damage to the head office, and repairs will be carried out within the next few days.

Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs

Planning Rural Credit Cooperatives

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, in order to help unemployed citizens in the city find ways to make a living, has established fifteen poverty relief loan offices since 1929. Last year, the amount loaned reached over 130,000 yuan, benefiting more than 10,000 poor people, with only eight yuan in bad debts. The results have been effective. After the war this year, the Jiangwan and Wusong districts suffered significantly, and the rural economy is facing even greater difficulties. In order to seek active relief, in addition to finding ways to restore the loan offices in each district, the bureau is planning rural credit cooperatives to facilitate the flow of the rural economy. Detailed regulations have been established for subsidies for cooperative expenses. A draft implementation plan for promoting rural credit cooperatives has been prepared and is being submitted to the Municipal Government for approval.

Last Batch of American Wheat Arrives in Shanghai

Last September, the National Government and the US authorities ordered 450,000 tons of relief wheat to relieve flood victims. The first batch arrived in Shanghai in mid-November, followed by subsequent shipments. Most of the wheat was unloaded at the China Merchants East Wharf in Pudong, and some was transported directly to various grain stations along the river for transshipment to the interior. The final batch of American wheat has arrived on the Coconut Wave steamer and is currently being unloaded at the Yangtze Warehouse, which will be completed today. The period from the arrival of the first batch to the last batch in Shanghai is approximately six months.

Northern District Business Community

Striving for Reduction or Exemption of Telephone Charges

Since the outbreak of the war, the shops on Avenue Edward VII have remained closed. The telephone company is collecting spring charges, and all users have appealed to the 30th branch of the Municipal Federation and the Business Federation of this road for exemption, or at least reduction of payment for the summer months. In addition to Director Song Shixiang of the association writing to the company, a letter has also been sent to the Taxpayers' Association for assistance in achieving the goal of reduction or exemption. It is also reported that there are plans to expand the organization of the Northern District Telephone Users' Association and notify users to register directly with lawyer Song at No. 731 Wanxiang Lane, Avenue Road, in order to strive for a united effort.

Huamao Real Estate Company Sues Tongchunfang Tenants

Tenants of Tongchunfang, located at the intersection of Zhejiang Road and Beihai Road, suffered losses from a two-month business suspension during the period when Japanese troops invaded the city and businesses closed to resist the invasion. They expressed that they would only pay the rental charges for February and March demanded by the landlord, Huamao Real Estate Company (managed by Elder), after the Shanghai Citizens' Rent Reduction Movement Committee reached a resolution and the issue was resolved by the Municipal Government Bureau. It is reported that the landlord has filed a lawsuit against seventeen tenant households for refusing to pay rent. The trial is scheduled to take place at 2:00 PM on the 19th in the First Special District District Court. In addition to hiring lawyer Le Junying to represent them in court, the tenants are also appealing for assistance from all walks of life. The case is expected to attract the attention of citizens throughout Shanghai.

Establishment of the Hatong Tenant Association

Yesterday, the Hatong tenants of this city held a founding meeting of the Tenant Association at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association. Over a hundred tenant representatives attended the meeting, and Lang Jingji, Le Fucheng, and Li Songtao were elected as the presidium, with Hong Xilin as the master of ceremonies and Cai Xiaohe as the recorder. After the customary formalities, the chairman first reported on the preparatory process, followed by the adoption of the articles of association and the election of executive committee members. Those elected were Lang Jingji, Le Fucheng, Gong Songtao, Gao Jiren, Jia Jingfang, Hong Xilin, Cai Baohe, Zhang Bingjun, Wu Wen'an, Fei Rongsheng, and Qian Huofo, totaling eleven members. Chen Zemin, Song Yunji, Yu Wen'an, and Zi Yiqing were elected as alternates. Next, proposals were discussed: (1) Regarding how to correct the landlord's outdated practice of collecting rent according to the lunar calendar, it was resolved that (a) according to city-wide practice, a request should be made to the landlord to change to paying rent according to the solar calendar from this year onward; (b) after changing to paying rent according to the solar calendar, the landlord must not use this as an excuse to increase the rent; (c) those who have already signed contracts with the landlord should also be changed to show equal treatment. (2) Regarding the request for rent reduction or exemption during the war period, it was resolved that (a) according to the resolution of the Shanghai Rent Reduction Movement Committee, a request should be made for two months of reduction or exemption to align with the rest of the city; (b) if the landlord comes to collect rent, payment should be delayed, but rent beyond the two-month period can be paid first. (3) and (4) omitted. (5) Regarding the proposal to issue a declaration at this representatives' conference, it was resolved to hand it over to the secretariat to draft it. Finally, Zhang Yichen, a representative of the Rent Reduction Movement Committee, provided guidance, and the meeting adjourned.

Another Opposition to Opium Monopoly

Overseas Chinese Federation Declaration

The Overseas Chinese Federation's Declaration Against Opium Monopoly states: "To the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association and all sectors of the nation: The harm of opium is known throughout the world, and all countries consider it a strict prohibition. However, our country's anti-smoking authorities and civil and military officials in various provinces are addicted to drugs, seeking only profit, abandoning smoking bans, and advocating public sales. Last year, the Anti-Smoking Investigation Bureau was in disarray for a time, but public opinion would not allow it, and opposition arose. The authorities then realized that public opinion could not be easily defied, and the Executive Yuan explicitly ordered its abolition. However, they disregarded the lessons of repeating past mistakes and sought to revive the dead ashes. They established a narcotic drugs management agency immediately afterward, but again suffered setbacks and failed to implement it. They accumulated hatred and malice, became ashamed and angry, and hoped to carry out a large-scale operation to satisfy their desires. Therefore, they recruited petty people, adopted evil schemes, and instructed various provinces to conduct public sales, causing the masses to be distracted and exhausted. The central anti-smoking authorities could both reap the benefits and shift the responsibility, and their cunning was unsurpassed. Currently, provinces across the country are implementing public sales in a rush, which has spread uncontrollably. It is said that only Zhejiang and Shandong provinces have not implemented it, while the rest are filled with opium addicts and enveloped in a poisonous fog. The sight is heartbreaking. What kind of world is this? At a time when foreign aggression has not ceased and the disaster of national extinction is imminent, the central government is busy defending against aggression and saving the nation, yet it has the audacity to implement this policy of poisoning the country and speeding up its demise. We overseas Chinese have yearned for good governance for twenty years. Although the Republic of China has not been entirely satisfactory, the hope that our motherland will one day strive for good governance and become strong has always lingered in our hearts without the slightest decrease. Now, the so-called National Government, which claims to be based on public opinion, is actually condoning various provinces and the central anti-smoking authorities in forcibly implementing the opium monopoly policy, which will destroy the nation and exterminate the race. This cannot but cause overseas compatriots to lose hope, break their hearts, and weep with despair, lamenting that there is ultimately no hope for the motherland. Opium monopoly is an evil policy of mercantile imperialism to poison the people of the colonies. We overseas Chinese, due to our commercial relations overseas, are entrusted to the rule of foreign powers and have personally tasted the bitterness of the colonial government's policy of drug promotion. The suffering is deeply ingrained in our minds. Our motherland's government, in order to appease the overseas Chinese, has promised to provide relief. However, not only has it gone back on its word, but it has also lost its mind and picked up the harsh policies of others. What others impose on colonies, we are now imposing on our own people, bringing shame for a hundred years, ridicule for ten thousand generations, and the disaster of extermination is imminent. Therefore, we dare to wipe away our tears and plead with all sectors of society to consider that the Chinese nation, which has survived and thrived for more than four thousand years, will from now on be dragged into the mire, enslaved, wailing in agony, and perishing together. We urge everyone to rise up and fight against the evil forces, one after another, even unto death, to punish all corrupt officials who promote drugs and extort wealth, and to kill all shameless traitors who advocate public sales, in order to create a precedent for the people's self-determination and save the nation from destruction. The Federation is willing to lead millions of overseas compatriots and vow to be the rearguard. We respectfully submit this declaration."

Seamen's Union Telegram Request

Recovery of Yangtze River Navigation Markers

Relates to National Defense, Do Not Delay and Mislead Again

The Reorganization Committee of the Chinese Seamen's Union telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters: "To the esteemed Central Executive Committee: It is our understanding that the Yangtze River navigation markers have been managed by the customs for decades without improvement. Hundreds of thousands of taels of tax are collected annually, but the convenience of shipping is not taken into consideration. The dredging of waterways, measurement of flow rates, indication of sandbars, hydrographic surveys, and installation of appropriate markers are all ignored. As a result, ships sailing in this area often run aground or run into sandbars. On May 6 of this year, the Shipping Weekly published an article expressing this concern in detail. Yangtze River merchant ships pay a large amount of ship tax every year, but the navigation markers in the inland ports are not maintained, making the merchant ships have the obligation to pay taxes but no benefit from navigation. Moreover, the Yangtze River is our country's inland river, but the navigation markers are managed by foreigners, who know the terrain like the back of their hand. This affects national defense and is no trivial matter. What is even more painful is that the customs provide convenience to foreigners but create difficulties for our country's ships. Seamen have personally experienced this and know it all too well. We read in the National Government's announcement of the Organizational Law of the Ministry of Transportation that navigation markers are under the jurisdiction of the Ministry, and we thought that they could be removed from customs management. However, the Ministry of Transportation has been delaying and misleading itself, allowing power to fall into the hands of others and become a guest in its own land, exceeding its authority, and the shipowners have been enduring it silently because they have no way to appeal. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has declared to the outside world that it will recover inland river navigation rights in 1932. Now is the time to recover the management of these navigation markers and return them to the competent department in order to maintain the law and be the vanguard of practicing the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' declaration. We have read in the newspapers that the Ministry of Transportation has requested the Executive Yuan to approve the recovery of management. We dare to present our concerns and earnestly request that the esteemed Committee forward this to the National Government and order the Executive Yuan to approve the proposed plan and order the Ministry of Finance to instruct the customs to quickly recover the management of these markers. This will not only greatly benefit the future of the shipping industry but also strengthen national defense. We respectfully submit this telegram and request your consideration." Respectfully, the Reorganization Committee of the Chinese Seamen's Union.

Diligence of Chinese Staff in Merchant Corps

Zhang Naibin Wins Shanxi Cup

The Shanghai International Merchant Corps Chinese Team makes an annual report on the performance of its members at the end of April to assess the performance of each member over the past year and determine rewards. The team often has competitions in team and individual shooting, and the members compete fiercely. The Shanxi Cup is particularly important. The cup was donated by General Li Tao'an of Shanxi to reward the member who has perfect attendance in all courses and the best shooting throughout the year. Therefore, it is not easy for those with more demanding duties to win this cup. The results of the team's members from the previous year have been announced. The member who has perfect attendance in all courses throughout the year and excels in all aspects is Sergeant Zhang Naibin, whose performance is the best in the entire team. Therefore, he has won the Shanxi Cup. In addition to having his name engraved on the cup, he will also receive a miniature cup for commemoration. It is reported that Zhang has been with the team for eight years and is usually known for his competence in his duties. During the Shanghai Incident, Zhang made outstanding contributions while the team was on defense. His enthusiasm and perseverance are truly commendable.

Drafting Regulations for the Organization of Employment Agencies

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, in view of the large number of unemployed people after the war, has long had the intention of establishing employment agencies. It has received an order from the Ministry of Industry to prepare for the establishment and has now drafted various articles of association, which have been submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and will be organized immediately.

Minutes of the Meeting of the Jiangxi Road Business Federation

The Jiangxi Road Business Federation, the 26th branch of the Municipal Federation, and more than a dozen members, including Xie Cheng, Shenghe, and Xinfu, jointly stated that they were being pressured to pay rent by the landlord Chen Zanting and requested that justice be upheld and assistance be provided. Yesterday, an emergency joint meeting was convened, attended by more than twenty people, including Zheng Dongshan and Qiao Tianlin. The resolutions are listed below: (1) Regarding the case of Yongjili Xiecheng and other firms being pressured to pay rent and pursued by the landlord Chen Zanting, requesting assistance: (a) a Yongjili Rent Reduction Committee will be organized; (b) Zhu Luhe, Zhang Tongfu, Yin Zhihe, Zhao Xianmin, and Wu Rongxing will be nominated as members; (c) letters will be sent to the Shanghai Rent Reduction Movement Committee, the Municipal Federation, and others requesting unified assistance; (d) Zheng Dongshan will be nominated to handle legal matters. (2) Regarding the request for exemption from telephone and water fees during the closure period, the resolution was passed.

Publication of Historical Diplomatic Materials from the Late Qing Dynasty

Mr. Huang Yanwang Taofu, while serving in the central government during the late Qing Dynasty, compiled a book titled "Historical Diplomatic Materials from the Late Qing Dynasty." His son, Xi Yin, has augmented and compiled it into a collection of 240 volumes. It also includes separate sections of indices and chronicles of important events during the Western Tour. It extensively collects documents and telegrams related to the formation of unequal treaties, war, peace negotiations, trade, and boundary demarcation during the Guangxu and Xuantong reigns, as well as meeting minutes from the Zongli Yamen (foreign affairs office) and foreign envoys. Every single piece of paper or fragment represents presently effective facts. It truly represents unprecedented diplomatic documents. It is reported that since its publication, domestic provinces such as Yunnan, Guizhou, and Xikang, as well as foreign countries such as Britain, the United States, France, Italy, the Netherlands, and Japan, have all subscribed to it. British and French individuals are even discussing translating the index into Western languages to broaden its circulation. Currently, with diplomacy being urgent, patriotic individuals overseas who intend to offer advice should quickly purchase a copy, as it will undoubtedly benefit national affairs.

Taihe Comprador Fined 8,000 Yuan

Shen Chengfu, the comprador of the British firm Taihe Foreign Company, absconded from his position last August due to a substantial deficit in the company's funds. The company's manager, a Westerner, hired a lawyer to sue him in the First Special District Local Court. Repeated trials have been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday morning was the date for the verdict in the case. Shen duly arrived in court as summoned. Judge Feng Shide ascended the bench and announced the main text of the judgment, stating that Shen Chengfu, knowing he had no deposits and without obtaining permission for overdrafts, issued checks, resulting in a fine of 8,000 yuan. If the fine is not fully paid through enforcement, the equivalent amount will be converted into imprisonment based on the ratio of the total fine to the number of days in a year. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be offset at a rate of three yuan per day. The charges of breach of trust and embezzlement were found not guilty. The attached civil suit will be transferred to the civil court. After the pronouncement, the police lawyer Wang Yaotang requested that the defendant remain under the original bail during the appeal period, which the court approved.

Nephew Sues Maternal Uncles

Embezzlement of Inheritance

Ten Shares Worth 300,000 Gold

Another Act in the Sheng Family Inheritance Dispute

After Sheng Zecheng and others divided the estate of their deceased mother, Madame Zhuang, their nephew, Lin Fengwen, not having received any share, sued his maternal uncles in the First Special District Local Court for embezzlement. Before one wave subsides, another rises. Now, he has been jointly sued by Shao Yunpeng, Yunqi, Yunlin, Yunxiang, Yunjun, and Yunzhi, the sons and daughter of his fourth aunt, Zhihui. Zhihui was the fourth daughter of Sheng Xuanhuai, married to a Mr. Shao from Yuyao. When Zhuang Tai Furen, the secondary wife of the late Vice-Minister, passed away in the sixteenth year, Zhihui personally attended to the funeral arrangements. Initially, there was no mention of Madame Tai Furen having a will for dividing the estate. Zhihui also passed away in the eighteenth year. Recently, during the opening of the trial in Lin Fengwen's lawsuit against Sheng Zecheng and others for embezzlement, the defendants stated that Madame Zhuang had left a will stating that Zhihui should receive 10,000 yuan, etc. The Shao sons only then learned of the existence of their maternal grandmother's will. Although their mother had also passed away, they were entitled to inherit this right according to the law. Considering that Madame Zhuang, during her lifetime, loved her children equally, the distribution of property should have been equal. The distribution amounts stipulated in the will showed obvious discrepancies. Therefore, the Shao brothers concluded that the will could not have originated from Madame Zhuang. As a result, the Shao brothers hired a lawyer to send letters to their maternal uncles Sheng Zecheng, Zechen, Pingchen, and their cousins Sheng Yuchang, Yuyou, and their aunts Sheng Guan Ying, Fang Yi, Ai Yi, Jing Yi, etc., questioning them. Failing to receive a satisfactory response, they followed in Lin Fengwen's footsteps and filed a criminal self-suit against their uncles and cousins, claiming that Madame Zhuang had a will for 3 million yuan, divided into ten shares, of which they should have jointly received 300,000 yuan. Because the defendants forged the will, the inheritance they were entitled to was entirely embezzled, and they requested a thorough investigation. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Tingqi of the First Special Court presided over the trial. The six plaintiffs designated Shao Yunpeng to state the purpose of the lawsuit. He claimed that the defendants had never informed them of the will or sent someone to summon Shao Xunmei, their adopted brother, after the property was divided, saying they would give each of them 10,000 yuan, but the talks were inconclusive. Sheng Zecheng, speaking for the defendants, stated that the will was discovered on October 31st of last year, so the distribution for each branch was handled according to the will thereafter. The plaintiffs' mother was supposed to receive 10,000 yuan, which was sent but rejected because they considered it too little. Judge Wu stated that because the parties were close relatives, it was inappropriate to be involved in litigation, and advised both parties to mediate outside the court. The case was adjourned to June 1st for further review.

Wang Zhenxiang Shot Dead in Revenge Attack

Formerly Involved in Flower Societies

Killed by Four Gunshots

Wang Zhenxiang (nickname "Little Devil Ah Liu"), a 33-year-old native of Shaoxing, residing at No. 10 Yukang Lane, Pi Shao Nai Road, French Concession, was formerly involved in flower societies. He was quite famous among the French Concession's gangsters and had considerable savings, owning a personal car. Around 12:45 AM this morning, Wang left his home after finishing a mahjong game with friends. Unexpectedly, four or five thugs, all dressed in blue cloth shirts and trousers, ambushed him in the alley. Seeing Wang step out of the alley entrance, the thugs immediately opened fire with pistols, firing about six or seven shots, hitting Wang four times: once in the side of his face, once in the abdomen, once in the left waist, and once in the left thigh. Wang fell to the ground in a pool of blood and died instantly. His wife rushed to the scene upon hearing the news, but the assailants had already fled without a trace. She immediately reported to the Songshan Road police station, who dispatched detectives to the scene. They could only transport the body to Renji Hospital for an examination before transferring it to Tongren Fu Yuan Tang for storage. The deceased was wearing a dark blue silk jacket, with a Sheng textile striped shirt and trousers underneath, black satin shoes, and gray silk socks. According to his wife, the deceased worked as the manager of Anle Hotel in Taiyuanfang. It is rumored that the suicide was related to marriage issues.

Notorious Bandit Fu Peisheng Cannot Escape the Law

Committed Numerous Crimes and Evildoings

To be Brought to Court Soon for Trial

The notorious bandit Fu Peisheng (nickname "Hua Mei Peisheng") usually robbed residents in the Gaoqiao area of Pudong. He had many accomplices. In the winter of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, he was arrested for leading a gang to rob Huang Shenqing's rice shop in Xujiaqiao, east of Gaoqiao, and was sentenced to three years in prison. After his release, he did not repent and continued to rob and extort in the countryside. Between the summer and autumn of last year, armed robberies in various towns and villages near Gaoqiao were almost nightly, causing the people to live in fear. These were all committed by the notorious bandit. Military police and various agencies sent out detectives to apprehend him. Eventually, with the help of Zhang Jinmao, a local villager, detectives captured four of Fu's gang members: Ni Erlang, Zhu Jinhua, Ge Sansan, and Zhu Jinfa. They were detained and interrogated by the headquarters. The bandits confessed directly that they obeyed the bandit leader Chuan Peisheng, carried out armed robberies at Xiaoshiqiao, Binwandou, and other places, robbing more than ten households of their property, and using the stolen money without denying it. The gang of bandits was sentenced to eight years of imprisonment, and Fu Peisheng and others were wanted by law. Afterwards, Fu Peisheng learned that the gang of bandits were caught by Zhang Jinmao, he hated him to the core. On the night of June 11th of last year, Fu Peisheng, together with the wanted Wu Chang Gui, Monk, and his concubine Guo Mao Lang, lured Zhang Jinmao to Jiebang in Gaoqiao Town. Fu Peisheng shot Jinmao in the back of the head, killing him instantly. Fu and others then used three large stones to tie Jinmao's body and sink it in the Jiebang River to destroy the body and cover up the traces. The next morning, the body floated up and was retrieved by local bailiffs, who reported it to the local court. Prosecutors were dispatched to the village to examine the body and provide a coffin for burial, while the criminal bandit Fu Peisheng and others were sought after. After killing Jinmao, Fu Peisheng and his concubine Guo Mao Lang fled to other places and only returned to Shanghai in the middle of last month. Zhang Quanzhou, a detective from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, arrested Fu Peisheng and Guo Mao Lang and sent them to the Third Section. Guo Mao Lang confessed that her concubine Fu Peisheng killed Zhang Jinmao, sank the body in the river, and fled to other places. The pistol was borrowed from his fellow party member Lu Ronglin. They are now being held in the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Upon hearing the news, the Shanghai Local Court has sent a letter to transfer them for trial.

Xie Jiwu Dies from Severe Injuries

Xie Jiwu, a native of Ningbo, was the comprador of the Zhaoshangju Guangji steamboat. He had considerable assets and lived at No. 31, Lane 282, Jing'an Temple Road. Around 6 PM on the afternoon of the 10th of this month, he suddenly committed suicide with a pistol at home. His family rushed him to Baolong Hospital for treatment. After a week, his injuries worsened, and he died in the hospital at 7:45 AM yesterday. At 2 PM in the afternoon, the court sent personnel to perform a preliminary examination. The body was transferred to the Wanguo Funeral Parlor for storage. The deceased, known as Lao Jiu, was 34 years old and had many friends in Shanghai. It is rumored that the suicide was related to marriage issues.

Jin Shoupei Dies Wrongfully

Mistakenly Shot by Bandits

Cao Qingcheng, a superintendent of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau from Ezhou, was assassinated by thugs with a gun at the entrance of Yongxing Lane, No. 184 Jiale Road, when he left his residence at No. 41 Yuancheng Lane, La Feide Road, French Concession around 1 PM on the 16th. He died on the spot. This has been reported in this newspaper. Jin Shoubei, a native of Jiangwan who lived at No. 25 in the same lane as Cao, happened to be seeing off a guest at the lane entrance at that time. The thugs mistook Jin's appearance for being the same as Cao's, and shot Jin in the back, with the bullet exiting from his chest. He was immediately sent to Guangci Hospital, but died in the hospital at 2 AM yesterday due to severe injuries. The hospital notified the police station, which sent detectives to take Jin's body to the Tongren Fu Yuan Branch Hall for examination. His mother, Jin Gu Shi, and wife, Ding Shi, were notified to report to the Second Special District Court today for an examination.

Report on the Issuance of Reserve by the Four Banks

No. 124

The Four Banks Reserve is jointly established by the Yanye Bank, Jin Cheng Bank, Zhongnan Bank, and Dalu Bank to handle the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the bank's issuance regulations, the issuance of banknotes is fully backed by reserves, with cash reserves accounting for at least 60% and guaranteed reserves accounting for at most 40%. A public announcement is made every week, and it is verified by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. Here is a record of the 124th announcement by the Shanghai Reserve on May 14, 21st year: Banknote circulation amount: 19,088,557 yuan. Total reserve amount: 19,088,557 yuan. Including: Cash reserve: 11,991,914.87 yuan. Guaranteed reserve: 7,096,642.13 yuan.

Dr. Tang Establishes Clinic in Shanghai

Dr. Tang Jiazhen studied in the United States, specializing in neurology and internal medicine. He served at Peking Union Medical College Hospital for many years. Based on his knowledge and experience, he founded the International Sanatorium in Qingdao and also served as the director of Qingdao Municipal Hospital. During the Anti-Japanese War of the 19th Route Army, Dr. Tang came to Shanghai overnight and established the 33rd Red Cross Wounded Soldier Hospital with his friends, and served at the First Wounded Soldier Hospital of the Citizens' Maintenance Association. Now that the war has gradually subsided, and many friends in Shanghai regret his departure, they have asked him to stay in Shanghai to establish a clinic. Dr. Tang has excellent knowledge and rich experience. He now has a clinic at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Mei Bai Ge Road. Clinic hours are from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM and 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM daily.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 3:30 PM yesterday: The Shandong coast will be cloudy with potential rain. Winds will come from varying directions between southwest and northwest. There will be cyclonic rain around the Korean peninsula, caused by a low-pressure system traveling in an east-northeast direction. The Yangtze River basin and the coast will be mostly cloudy, with unstable winds. The East China Sea will be cloudy, with relatively strong winds coming from varying directions between southeast and southwest. The area around Hainan Island will have bad weather, caused by a small hurricane traveling in a northwest direction. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the local temperature was a high of 84.6 and a low of 68.4. On the same day last year, the high was 60.6 and the low was 55.8.

Letters to the Editor

Dear Editor,

Regarding the article on page 3 of your newspaper on the 16th of this month, concerning the case of Dr. Tang Jingqing from Nanshi being intimidated, it mentions Wang Zuzhen, 25 years old, from Zhenhai, currently working as an accountant at the Salt Affairs Audit Office, who claims to be the main culprit in this case. After investigation, there is no such person as Wang Zuzhen working in our office as an accountant. This is clearly fabricated. We hereby request that you correct it immediately. Sincerely, the Salt Affairs Audit General Office of the Ministry of Finance, Shanghai Newspaper Office, May 18th, No. 987.

Dear Editor,

Regarding the news in the "Local News" section on page 9 of issue No. 3 of your newspaper on May 6th ("Mutual Admiration in Hospital, Widow Lives Together"), it states that Yang Xianbang, the former head of surveying for the Gongxun Bureau, is currently serving as a road consultant in the Henan Security Office, etc. After investigation, Yang Xianbang is not an advisor in several locations, and there is no such person as Yang Xianbang among the employees. We hereby request that you investigate and correct this matter. Sincerely, the Henan Security Office to the Shanghai Newspaper Office, May 12th.

Dear Editor,

According to Mr. Yang Jingcun, the person concerned, today's newspapers published a news item about Kong Chenshi Kong Shujun suing me in court for inflicting harm. After reading it, I was deeply surprised. Although this case has been summoned for questioning once, it was postponed due to my late arrival and has not yet been publicly tried. However, the newspapers were able to describe the opposing party's statement in detail, as if they were familiar with it. This clearly shows that the opposing party intentionally spread propaganda in an attempt to damage my reputation. I hereby request that you issue a statement to the newspapers on my behalf, stating that Kong Shujun, who is actually Miaodi Laoqi, has been engaged in prostitution and has no marital relationship with me. The statements made in her complaint are purely fabricated and do not correspond to the facts. Please correct this matter promptly to avoid confusing the public. Sincerely, Lawyer He Shimei to the Chief Editor of the Shanghai Newspaper Office.

Dear Editor,

Regarding the article "University Students Mistaken as Koreans" that our agency sent to your newspaper on the 14th of this month, the French Concession police station on Songshan Road claims that this is not factual. We hereby request that you correct this matter urgently. Sincerely, the National News Agency to the Chief Editor of the Shanghai Newspaper. May 18th.

Business News

Gold and Silver Prices Rebound Four Taels

The market was extremely calm yesterday. The gold price situation was quite peaceful. The total amount of gold changing hands throughout the day was only four taels. Looking back, it has broken through 700 taels again, with an overall increase of around four taels. Prices rose from the beginning, although large bars continued to increase, the silver price actually fell back. In the future, there may be slight ups and downs, but as the foreign exchange situation seems tense, the gold price is likely to be mediocre, with only a slight drop, due to Wednesday being a non-trading day. Transactions from all sides were also scarce, but the market sentiment was stable. The daily situation is recorded below:

Breaking Through the 700 Tael Mark

The July opening price rose four and a half taels to 702.5 taels. The British silver price continued to rise by one-eighth, while the American silver price fell by one-quarter. Private telegrams were the same. The market situation was reported to be stable. Then, due to purchases by Tongchang Hengyu, Dadecheng Zhifengyong, etc., it increased by another tael to 03.5 taels. Zhifengyong retreated to 02.2 taels, but then Yuanheng Qianchang Xiang Bingxing and others came to buy, and the China Bank absorbed 31.5 yuan in June U.S. dollars, while Mai Bank absorbed the current period for 4,375 and August British gold for 625, so the price rebounded by more than two taels, reaching 04.8 qian at 9:20 AM. At this time, retail investors sold off, with Sun selling at 1.23 qian, and the British gold opening price had narrowed by one grade, with the U.S. dollar at 375, resulting in 04.5 qian. After a moment, there were ups and downs of 1.67 qian. Dalian dealers sold while Zhifengyong bought. When the internal price stabilized, Bombay offered May British gold at 18.5, with a forward price of 18.625. Until after 10:30, Yuanmaoyong Yuanda Yongshunli Wanxing Yuantai, etc., came to sell, and the U.S. dollar for September was quoted at 32.0625 with both buying and selling available. Sanjing sold August silver for 875, so the gold price fell sharply by four taels. At 11:00, it was 700 taels and 0.05 qian. After that, Yifeng Yongfu Taiheng Fuyu bought, so it was pulled up by more than two taels to 03.2 qian at 11:45. Before long, Hengyu Richang and others sold, and it depreciated by one tael to the noon closing price of 01.9 qian. The quoted price was changed to 777 taels, with a discount of 73 to 75.6 taels.

Mediocre Afternoon Market with No Special Changes Afternoon Market Opens at 01

Taels and six qian. Xie Xingyong and others sold off, losing seven or eight qian. At 2:30, it was 01 tael. Yuanmaoyong and others brought in, at 2:45, it was 01 tael and seven qian, but the potential was small. Zhifengyong and Yifengyong sold off, and at 3:30, it suddenly became 700 taels and 0.01 qian. At this time, Yuanmaoyong Bingxing and others made slight purchases, and it rose by two taels. Until 4:00, it was 02 taels, but the ups and downs were extremely small, only a few qian. Soon after, retail investors sold off, and after ten minutes, it lost only six qian, to 01 tael and four qian. Qianchang Xiang Fuxingyong and others entered the market and pulled it up by three or four qian. At 4:30, it was 01 tael and eight qian, a rebound of 3.8 qian compared to the day before, but items were sold, so it was small within one tael (items were 8 qian smaller).

Quoted Price Discount of 75.6 Taels

According to the daily maximum of 704.8 taels and the minimum of 700.01 taels, there was a difference of 4.7 qian. The quoted price was discounted by 75.6 taels. Registered loans were 705 taels for May and June, 02 taels for July, and a supplementary water fee of 705 taels. Red bars were increased by ten taels.

Scattered Transactions

On the trading floor, Yuanheng, Qianchangxiang, Bingxing, Yuhe, Futaiheng, Taifengcheng, and Yifengyong all bought, while Wanxing, Shunli, Yuanmaoyong, Yuantai, and Fuxingyong all sold. Yarn and Cotton

Weak Yarn Market

The yarn market is exceptionally sluggish with nothing exciting to report. Some are bearish due to the rapid changes in the situation in Guangdong and the unrest in Japan not being fully resolved. With these various factors, the yarn market is in a state of siege on all sides, so how can there be any vitality? Therefore, most people are adopting a selling-off strategy. Fortunately, the bottom has already been reached. Even if major unfavorable news comes out, the degree of market decline is still shallow. However, actual sales have also become sluggish, and it is difficult for the market to turn around.

Eighteen Taels Lower Than Last Year

Yesterday, the new black tea from Wenzhou arriving from the LUZHUANG (Road Estate) was opened by Jardine Matheson at a starting price of 31 taels, 2 mace, and 5 fen, 18 taels lower than last year. Qimen black tea was also priced at 31 taels, 2 mace, and 5 fen, 18 taels lower than last year, but no deals have been made. The continued rise of foreign silver prices has increased interest from British tea merchants, leading to a more bullish market. However, there were no significant transactions for both LUZHUANG (Road Estate) and TUZHUANG (Native Estate) Jane-Mei green teas. The price of LUZHUANG (Road Estate) Suei-An tea fell by more than 10 taels, creating an unfavorable situation, it is said.

Wuyuan Extracted-Core Tea Has Begun Production

Wuyuan green tea, with its excellent quality and taste, is the highest-grade green tea among foreign estate teas produced in China. With a wide variety of types, the most prized is Jane-Mei. In recent years, various tea houses, in order to gain recognition for Chinese tea worldwide, have invented a type of Extracted-Core Jane-Mei. Both the selection of materials and the production method are extremely refined. Last year, foreign merchants offered up to 350 taels for the Extracted-Core tea from Dongxiang, a market price rarely seen since tea production began in Wuyi County. As a result, Wuyi tea's reputation shone brightly in Europe and America. This year, the tea houses along the eastern route are striving for even greater perfection and are paying special attention to the Extracted-Core tea. Before the new tea season even started, they sent personnel to famous tea-producing areas to search for green buds and tender tips, offering prices ranging from one yuan to one yuan and three or four jiao per catty, making the tea cost over 400 yuan. The price of the tea plants in the mountains is even higher than that of Qimen tea. The Jinzhu Jitai Tea House in northern Wuyi began selecting and producing Extracted-Core tea the day before yesterday (the 9th). The tea's tenderness, color, aroma, and taste are all present. The tea is called "Fragrant Herb" and should be ready to be packed in boxes in about ten days. It is predicted that when this batch of Extracted-Core tea arrives in Shanghai, it will surely impress foreign merchants deeply.

Qimen Black Tea Market Price Declines

Qimen Fuqiu black tea could normally be completely harvested by now, but since the tea season began, it has not rained for several days, and it has often been cold. As a result, it is difficult to call tea production prosperous, and tea houses are rarely buying. Although the two- or three-character teas are currently being shipped, the tea houses are hoping for sunny weather in the coming days to improve tea production so they can buy more. However, the sun has not appeared for the past two days, and there has been heavy rain. The tea produced is coarse, loose, and bulky. Furthermore, the tea houses have received telegrams from Shanghai stating that the financial situation is still tight and that the foreign tea market has not improved, advising them to be cautious and buy less. Upon receiving this news and struggling with a lack of cash, the tea houses have stopped weighing and buying tea, causing the mountain price to fall by 30 yuan compared to the previous few days. The market has suddenly become sluggish, with supply exceeding demand. Currently, the first-character tribute teas from various tea houses are being shipped one after another. The first-character large batches should be stacked up and ready for transport within a few days. Approximately ten days later, a large quantity of new tea should be on the market.

Pessimistic Outlook for Silkworm Season in Pinghu

Recently, the development of silkworms has been hindered by cold weather in various villages and towns in Pinghu and Dayi. The degree of hindrance varies from place to place. Early batches have already completed their major molt and started eating leaves, while later batches are still in their second molt. The poor weather is affecting the molting season. This year's silkworm production has already declined compared to the past due to the impact of the Shanghai war. Furthermore, economic difficulties have led to a shortage of money to buy leaves. As a result, many are abandoning their silkworms. There is an oversupply of mulberry leaves, and no one is interested in buying them. Therefore, people are going to the villages to peddle them. The price of leaves is around one yuan. The poor harvest of silkworms this year is already a proven fact and will have a significant impact on commerce. It is hoped that the authorities will find a way to provide relief.

Low Price Ceiling for New Cocoons in Hangzhou

New cocoons in Hangzhou have already entered the market. Large cocoon firms have set a price ceiling for today (the 18th)

Because of the relationship, the story suppresses, hearing the high goods limit 30 yuan, so the general sales cocoon villagers, Mo does not mourn the shape in color, saying that the leaf is still not the grain.

No Improvement in Foreign Estate Silk Sales

Yesterday, the foreign estate silk market in Shanghai showed no improvement. Foreign silk telegrams remained unfavorable, and American and European estates were thinking of accumulating cheap goods. However, Chinese silk merchants, due to substantial losses, were waiting and not selling, creating a stalemate in the market. Factory white, yellow, and gray silks remained stagnant due to low prices. The future of the silk market continues to look bleak.

Yesterday, several rice trading groups in southern Shanghai received ships numbered 34. River port inventories were low. Due to the clearing weather, people settled their expectations, and retail sales in cities and villages increased. The prices of Changzhou, Wuxi, northern japonica, and Suzhou and Tongzhou rice arriving in the market remained unchanged. The inventory of early and late rice was slightly higher, but sales were slow, and the market price remained stable but sluggish. High-quality Yanglu rice was scarce, and the market remained stable.

Yesterday, several rice trading groups along the Suzhou Creek in northern Shanghai received ships numbered 56. The market in the city and along the waterway was initially active but then weakened. Transactions for Changzhou and Wuxi white japonica and Kunshan and Jiangyin rice were sluggish, with prices falling by about 1 jiao. High-quality green-tip, Shibu, and Songjiang rice remained relatively stable. The price of customs-controlled rice fell by 2 jiao. There were no gains or losses for Yanglu and glutinous rice.

Pickled Mussels are Scarce

Xutou Woolen Fabrics: Popular Items Unwilling to Lower Prices

Sales of woolen fabrics are gradually becoming slow, and prices are trending downwards. Suppliers have various difficulties and must adopt a sacrificial attitude to sell goods for cash. Yesterday, the weather in Shanghai suddenly became hot, and trading became even quieter. Buyers are not interested in cheap goods that are not in season. However, suppliers are unwilling to lower prices for items such as Huate woolen fabrics and Jiji straight tribute fabrics, as these are popular items that can be sold in all seasons. Therefore, they are willing to store them and sell them at good prices in the fall. Most of the woolen goods currently offered for sale are likely to incur losses. Although some may make a profit, it is ultimately not possible to break even. Woolen fabric stores are not placing orders with foreign firms and are selecting and buying spot goods on the market.

Hardware: English Tinplate Prices Rise by 2.5 Mace

It is said that over 1,000 boxes were traded yesterday, and buyer interest remains strong, indicating the potential for continued improvement in the market.

Although the supply from overseas is not large, the current inventory in Shanghai is still abundant. Therefore, it is difficult to expect progress in the future, it is said.
