Free Talk

The Life of Ōkura (Part 1)

— Kai Xu

1932. Truly a most unfortunate year in history, wasn’t it? Why were there so many incidents? This year bore the brunt of the economic downturn of various countries. The entire globe suddenly displayed an image of instability. Unprecedented disturbances occurred in both politics and economics. And prominent figures from various countries also passed away one after another in this year. Now, Mr. Ōkura has also passed away. He lived for eighty-eight years. He was a kind and amiable person who dedicated half his life to the shipping industry in the Far East. Many Chinese people knew him well. Now, unfortunately, he has passed away. I am writing a brief outline of his life as follows.

Ōkura’s full name was Captain Robert D. Dollar. He was born in 1844 in Falkirk, Scotland. His family made a living from seafaring. During his lifetime, three of his uncles died at sea. The ships they were on sank between Bombay and Calcutta, India, due to storms. All three perished. At the age of twelve, Ōkura abandoned his studies and became employed in a machine factory. His salary was only half a crown per week. When Ōkura first received it, he ran ecstatically for dozens of miles to present it to his mother. Ōkura lived extremely frugally, and he always saved his earnings. His mother passed away not long after. Overwhelmed with grief, his father often indulged in alcohol. According to Ōkura’s autobiography, his family moved to Canada around this time. And because he witnessed his father’s addiction to alcohol, he vowed to abstain from it for life. Ōkura kept his vow throughout his life. In recent years, every time it was his birthday, when newspaper reporters would ask him for a word, he would always say that the key to his lifelong success was based on abstaining from alcohol. When the Ōkura family moved to Canada, Ōkura was still a fourteen-year-old boy. After arriving in Canada, he initially worked in a barrel factory and then switched to working as a lumberjack in the forest. At this time, he always focused on increasing his knowledge while working. Later, he was promoted to foreman. By this time, he had accumulated some savings. However, his fate was not good. He invested all of his savings of five thousand dollars in the lumber business. Unfortunately, it failed, and he lost all his capital. Around 1880, Ōkura moved his family to a village in Michigan, USA. He established a sawmill there. The area gradually developed into what is now the city of Dollarville. With his savings, he gradually purchased public land nearby. His family’s foundation grew stronger. Soon after, he moved to California in pursuit of greater advancement. Initially, he was engaged in transporting timber to neighboring ports. Later, as the business expanded, he gradually realized that the lack of seagoing vessels was a major obstacle to the future of his business. However, after his uncles were buried at sea, Ōkura was unwilling to continue in the seafaring business. At this point, he seemed to be driven by the inherited adventurous spirit of his family and decided to revive the old business. In fact, he initially only regarded the shipping business as a sideline to his timber transportation. He never expected that today it would become a shipping business that dominates the world.

The Resting Giant

— Ying Ge

丨 Random Writings from the Old Capital - Three 丨

Walking into the front gate city cave, which resembles the nostril of a giant, you arrive inside the city walls. Opening your eyes, everything is black, with only sparse streetlights and the clocks on the tips of the tall buildings emitting a little light. Because I was unfamiliar with the route and lacked snow gear, I had to rely on a middle-aged rickshaw puller. After agreeing on a mutually acceptable fare, I sat in the rickshaw and headed to my desired destination.

The snow on the ground had already accumulated more than a foot deep. There were very few vehicles and pedestrians on the road. Only the policemen, faithful to their duty, stood like stone Buddhas in the middle of the road. The old capital, this black giant, was resting peacefully at this moment.

The rickshaw pulled me across a long street. Both ends of the street had iron gates. Several cars were parked on the street, quiet and clean, just as I had imagined. In my heart, I was happy about this, feeling that the old capital, after all, did not fail to be the former capital. The municipal administration of the former capital was so beautiful! Just as I was about to sing its praises, I was caught off guard by the sound of singing from the roadside. I quickly looked over and saw a soldier in a green uniform, holding a sharp rifle, strolling leisurely under a building flying the Union Jack. I suddenly realized that this was the East Legation Quarter. Immediately, a general sense of resentment drove away the joy that had just emerged in my heart. Yes, on the pulse of this diseased great power of East Asia, there is no place where brutal snakes and scorpions are not active.

The Sugar Poison Plot

— Jing Mengdie

Late spring weather, green grass south of the Yangtze River. Everywhere, the sound of tin flutes urges people into afternoon naps. This is the flavor of the countryside, the old customs of our country. Unexpectedly, those inhuman Japanese pirates actually hide their sinister plots here, in order to harm our innocent and carefree little citizens. Two weeks ago, when the ceasefire agreement had not yet been signed, in the countryside south of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, there were peddlers carrying sugar on shoulder poles. They came blowing short flutes. Village children gathered upon hearing the sound. The peddlers then set down their loads and stood there, first taking sugar and distributing it to the children, one piece to each child. When the children took out money to buy it, the amount of sugar they received was several times more than usual. Therefore, children everywhere competed to buy it, and business was particularly prosperous. One day, in Xu Village between Yixing and Jintan, children died one after another. Upon investigation, it was discovered that it was because of eating the sugar. The villagers then gathered a crowd to arrest the sugar peddlers. They caught eight people, tied them to trees, and interrogated them. They confessed everything. They were also a kind of traitor. Five people shared a boat, and each boat received a daily allowance of thirty silver dollars. The sugar was also distributed by the Japanese and required no capital. The Japanese also ordered these people to choose the gates of village elementary schools as their market, in order to target the concentrated points of children for a complete roundup, achieving twice the results with half the effort. Driven by life, they had to act as accomplices to the tigers. Moreover, because the Japanese secretly monitored them very strictly, after receiving orders, they had no choice but to carry out the killings. The villagers then questioned them about what kind of poison was placed in the sugar and whether there was any antidote. They replied that the poisoning would not cause immediate death but could be delayed for ten days. If pig liver and wild chives were eaten, it could be resolved. After the villagers escorted the eight traitors to the authorities, they urgently searched everywhere for wild chives and purchased pig liver. For a time, the slaughterhouses could not meet the demand, and the price of pig liver soared to two silver dollars per pound. This matter instantly spread everywhere, and everyone who heard the news was shocked. City tigers and grass snakes were startled, and even non-poisonous sugar was rejected and not allowed to be sold in the villages.

Chronicle of World Events

— Hai Ke

There is a new plan between the United States of America and Canada for the Peace Garden. In order to maintain the permanent friendship between the two countries, they plan to build a Peace Garden to celebrate the peace and friendship of over a hundred years between the two countries. The area of the garden is approximately one thousand acres, with half of the location in the United States and half in Canada, generally in the area of Manitoba and North Dakota. The citizens of both countries have expressed warm sympathy for this plan. It has been decided that all the flowers and trees planted in the garden will be products of both countries, and a very large glass greenhouse will be built. The total cost of construction and planting is estimated at £200,000, and another £300,000 will be raised for permanent maintenance costs. It is truly a very good example for the current world that neighboring countries can express friendship and not invade each other in this way. Especially for our country, which has been wantonly trampled upon by the iron hooves of neighboring countries, we cannot help but admire it.

Shanghai's Great Sale

— Sun Guliang

Stepping out the door, you stand at the intersection of Nanjing Road. No matter where you look, your eyes are filled with "Great Sale" banners!

Sales happen every year, but this year is very different! It’s really a sale after sale, and after one sale ends, another one starts. It’s continuous, regardless of wind or rain, vast and abundant, forming a grand spectacle. It fully demonstrates the Shanghai of great sales!

Is this a sign of economic collapse after the war? Perhaps every store feels this pain! In fact, this is an objective "outsider's criticism"! Looking at the exchange rates of silver and interest rates after the war, they have fallen to the lowest possible levels. Can it be said that there is economic collapse after the war?

Our financial elder statesmen who are supposed to regulate the social economy are wearing short-sighted old glasses and don't care about these things. Their only creed and authority is to have made tens of thousands this year, holding the "red ledger," sitting in a carriage, and going to curry favor with Lao Chang!

Some say, "Your words are too extreme. Isn't our only Shanghai also on a great sale? Isn't the ceasefire agreement an invoice given to others? I advise you to turn your pen and first supervise the government, which is responsible for regulating land and has recently sold off Shanghai at a great discount!"

Hearing this, I was stunned, feeling that these words were very good. I couldn't help but secretly pray that the great sale of Shanghai would end, hoping that there would not be a great sale of China.

Records of What I Heard and Saw in the Old Capital—Zhu An

— Yu De Tang

Entering the Xihua Gate to view the books and paintings stored in the Ancient Artifacts Exhibition Hall, one arrives at Wuying Hall. Northwest of the hall are three small halls, labeled Yude Tang. The hall has a bathroom. Outside the bathroom is a well pavilion, as high as the hall. In the pavilion is a well, made of brick and stone. Square water pipes run along the back of the hall, passing to the east to the bathroom. The roof of the bathroom is round like a lid. The square water pipes from the well connect directly to it. To the side is a small door with iron bars. A brick platform has steps to climb. This platform is for placing an iron cauldron to boil water, clearly visible. The four walls of the room are all tiled with white glazed bricks. It is neither a Chinese object nor modern architecture. Upon careful consideration, it is likely that Wuying Hall was originally a place for technical specialists from faraway lands to await summons. Printing books with movable type was done here, foreign languages were taught here, and specialized books were compiled here. This must have been a Turkish bathing method presented by Muslims, and the order was given to imitate its style here, merely to broaden knowledge of strange things. However, popular tradition says that Emperor Gaozong favored a certain Uyghur concubine because of her unique fragrance, calling her the Fragrant Concubine, and therefore imitated her country's customs to build a bathing hall. However, it is not considered that Wuying Hall was the outer court and certainly not a place that concubines could reach, let alone bathe. Common people are unfamiliar with national affairs, ignorant of historical events, and often make wild guesses, and those who learn by hearsay also believe deeply without doubt. It is truly laughable. Emperor Gaozong had a Uyghur concubine, and the rumors have been around for a long time. Wang Kaiyun's Xiangqilou Wenji, in the "Biographies of Notable Women" section, recorded what he heard. This is originally not surprising, but it should not be attached to Yude Tang.

… expose it to sunlight. However, the weather is unpredictable. There is a lot of rain in the south of the Yangtze River. If it is overcast for ten days, the fungus will spread more and more. It is a pity to watch them die. Moreover, the fine varieties are not easy to obtain, with each fish costing more than its weight in gold. We love and protect them. How can we allow them to be wiped out? This year, Mr. Dong spent four gold coins to obtain a double-tailed dragon variety, several inches long and pleasingly plump. The other day, one fish suddenly floated sideways on the water surface, looking like it was about to die. Mr. Dong was shocked and asked me for a remedy. I carefully examined the disease and found that it was abdominal fungus, with scales that could be vaguely pointed out. This was easier to treat than gill rot, but due to continuous rain, sunlight therapy was impossible. I jokingly told him, "People with illnesses can use artificial sun lamps. Perhaps it is also possible for fish. Why not use the huge light bulbs that your company's sound film studio recently purchased from the United States and shine them on the fish? Perhaps it can be saved." Mr. Dong agreed. It so happened that they were filming the sound film "Tears and Laughter" every night. He consulted with the electricians and took the sick fish, placed them in a small container, and put them in clear water. He shone the light on them. In less than half an hour, the fish that was lying on its side gradually straightened up. Then, he added a little salt and applied it to the affected area, shining the light on it again. In less than three hours, it swam freely. The fungal area showed a slight charred blackness. The next day, sunlight appeared, and he exposed it to the sun again. For the past few days, the previous illness seems to have disappeared, and it is chasing its old companions, competing for food among the algae and looking for red worms.

The Romance of Rongma Shuanglou (56)

— Master of the Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter Seven: Seeking an Audience with the Powerful Often Makes Generals Fall; Imprisoned in the Prison of Love, Even Jailers Can Become Husbands

Liang Xiaoyun thanked Fifth Madam for her flattery. After sitting for a while, she got up to take her leave. Fifth Madam wanted to keep her to go out and watch the show together. She still insisted that she had things to do at home and would accompany her another day. Fifth Madam smiled and said, "I understand. Newlyweds are too deeply in love and can't bear to be apart for even a moment. I won't force you to stay." Saying that, she picked up a small black velvet box from the bedside and handed it to her, saying, "You should still take this back. It's your joyous occasion. How can I accept such a precious object from you before sending you a gift?" Liang Xiaoyun repeatedly refused, saying, "Sister, you can't be so polite with me. This little thing is nothing. It's not like I specially bought it as a gift. You know everything. How can you not give me face? Besides, my husband and I will rely on you for a long time in the future. If you are still so distant, how can I come and bother you to ask for help in the future?" Fifth Madam listened to her earnest words and changed her tone, saying, "You and I are sisters. Being good to each other isn't just for one day. There's no need for formality. Since you say so, it would seem wrong of me not to accept it. Then I'll thank you. As for your husband's matter, don't worry. I'll urge the old man to take care of it. You might as well bring him over one day soon." Saying this, she showed a very concerned expression and called Deshun in, instructing him, "Tomorrow, pay attention to see if the Marshal has time to meet guests. If there's a chance, quickly take the car to Miss Eight's residence to pick up Mr. An and bring him to see the Marshal. It would be best if you could come along, too." Deshun respectfully agreed. Liang Xiaoyun also expressed her gratitude and took out two hundred yuan in banknotes, handing them to Deshun, saying, "Half of this is for you to keep for spending money. As you are now, it's much more promising than following your father playing the erhu in the hall. You play the moon guitar and accompany him. You should really be grateful for Fifth Madam's promotion. You should serve her well in the future. The other half, please distribute it to the old maids in the room for me. Tomorrow, you'll have to work harder." Deshun grinned and dared not accept it. Fifth Madam said, "Sister, what are you doing again?" Liang Xiaoyun smiled and said, "It's just a small token. Sister, tell Deshun to accept it."

Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao

Words

Circular Evolution

— Buddha

There are several theories among philosophers regarding the evolution of mankind. One is gradual, one is spiral, and one is cyclical. Until the end, no one can definitively say which is correct.

In the era of primitive humans, people lived in caves and the wilderness. Marriage systems had not yet emerged, and men and women intermingled, no different from beasts. Later, as civilization progressed, marriage systems became stricter.

According to recent reports, eighty women in Vienna held their secret rituals in the mountains near Bisallaia’s Paternia. This ritual belongs to a new Protestant sect that calls itself the “Innocent.” What a “naive” term! Since the eastward expansion of European culture, the culture of our country has progressed by leaps and bounds. For example, women mostly bare their chests and wear tight clothes and short pants, fully displaying their rich sensuality and beautiful curves. Even men and women bathe together without considering it to be strange, although they still wear bathrobes, which are not entirely nude. But in the innocent, there is still some affectation. If civilization were to progress more, it would be the same as in primitive times.

Therefore, the most "innocent" was the era of primitive people. The course of civilized evolution is indeed circular. This can be used as evidence.

Withered Spring Shen, great calamity fallen,

Cold Shanghai, the grasses of Wusong do not spring.

Shattered rivers and mountains, sorrowful gaze,

Scattered homeland, trapped in barbarian dust.

Endless sad memories, New Pavilion weep,

Planning to visit the central stream, strike the oar.

Mourning the Fallen Soldiers of the Nineteenth Route Army

I still remember holding the halberd horizontally at Jiangwan that night,

Knowing that your heroic souls are concerned with the nation's thoughts,

In the underworld, you must be shedding tears of sorrow.

Falling flowers and rain mixed at dusk,

Elders offering pots of wine, tears welling.

Death's honor is heavier than Mount Tai,

Relying on a cup of wine to mourn the loyal souls.

Science

Artificial Rubber

— Yuan He

Rubber is formed by the solidification of the latex of special plants, produced in South America, East India, West India, and Africa, etc. Initially, it was only collected by the natives of South America, and few knew its uses. In 1615, the European Teande Torquemade invented waterproof clothing made of rubber. In 1770, the Englishman Priestty discovered that rubber could erase pencil marks. After several studies, its use became more obvious, not only making it into rubber cloth, but also making it soft and making various models.

Since the American Nelson invented the vulcanization method, the function of rubber has been fully utilized, and it has become an indispensable raw material in industry. According to the 1910 survey by Dr. p. Schibrowitty, the world's rubber supply has reached a huge 81,000 tons, which shows its position in manufacturing. In modern times, natural rubber has become more in demand than supply for industrial raw materials. Therefore, there are artificial rubber inventions.

There are many kinds of artificial rubber manufacturing methods. The simplest and easiest method is to mix two parts of coarse linseed oil, one part of black he oil, and fry them until they can be pulled into silk. Then add half a part of finely ground linseed oil that has been fried to a thick consistency. For every 100 parts of the fried product, add one-twelfth part of sperm whale oil and one-twelfth part of ground wax, and fry it at a heat of 252 degrees (Kolon table). Then add one-twelfth part of sulfur. After it cools, it becomes artificial rubber.

Artificial Ivory

Artificial ivory is white in color and firm in quality. It can be used for various carvings. It is suitable as a raw material for small crafts. It is cheap and beautiful. Here are the most convenient methods for those who are interested in this.

(1) Peel the skin of the potato and soak it in dilute sulfuric acid solution. After 36 hours, take it out and wrap it with non-glue paper to make it dry. Then put it into the mold and add external pressure. It will be done. However, it must be noted that water should be gradually added to the sulfuric acid solution to dilute it, otherwise, it may be dangerous, because sulfuric acid can generate great heat.

(2) Mix seven ounces of eggshell powder and three ounces of gypsum powder evenly, and grind them with fish glue and water. Put them in a mold coated with lard. After seven days, take them out and make them dry, and they will be no different from fish teeth. Some also mix one ounce each of fine eggshell powder and fish glue brandy, adjust the temperature slightly, and stir evenly to make a mud. Put it in the mold. After the heat dissipates, it becomes solid ivory.

Nonsense

Explaining the Constellations

— Shibin

Mrs. Li thought that her family had recently been stolen, losing more than a thousand yuan, and that her husband had received a threatening letter last month. She thought that her husband's fate had not been good recently, so two unsatisfactory things happened one after another. She had to find a highly skilled fortune teller to tell her husband's fortune. Just as she was thinking this, her nanny brought in a flyer, saying that a fortune-telling hall had newly opened on Chengdu Road, and the fortune teller was very accurate. No matter how bad or good the fortune was, he could calculate it. Mrs. Li was right in the middle of her thoughts when she heard the nanny's words. She immediately went out and called the rickshaw puller A San to quickly pull her to Mr. × on Chengdu Road.

Stepping into the fortune-telling hall, an old man in his fifties came up to greet her, saying that those who want their fortunes told should first register, and the fortune-telling fee and registration fee together were two cents. Mrs. Li gave the money. She saw that in the middle of the reception hall, there was a small square table on which there were incense burners, divination tubes, scrolls, etc. In the center sat a blind man in his thirties.

Mrs. Li explained the eight characters. The blind man turned his hand around and muttered a bunch of gibberish, saying, "If this eight characters are calculated according to the exact Yin hour, then the person is very strong and aggressive. If they are soft, then it is the beginning of the Yin hour, because one hour has three quarters, upper, middle, and lower. Madam, how exactly is this person? If you make a mistake with the time, the calculation will not be accurate."

"His temper is still okay. Everyone below says he is amiable," Mrs. Li replied to the blind man. "Then I will calculate it according to the fortune. Madam, listen carefully. This fortune is at the beginning of the Yin hour. The person is very peaceful, has food to eat, and has some family property. He doesn't need to look for food..." The blind man hadn't finished speaking when Mrs. Li smacked her lips and said, "That's right."

The blind man had previously heard from the people below that he was amiable, and he had already determined that he was a wealthy household. Now, after hearing Mrs. Li say this, he already had a plan in mind. Wealthy households have food to eat. Why would they come to have their fortunes told? Something big must have happened to make them think of having their fortunes told. So he continued, "Although this fortune has a lot of family property, it hasn't been good recently. It looks like you've lost a lot of money."

"Ah! Sir, you're really like a deity. A theft has already occurred, and thousands of yuan were stolen. But what will happen in the future?"

"Looking at the eight characters, I'm afraid you've lost more than a thousand yuan. It's still not enough. This fortune is really bad. I'm afraid you'll even see a threatening letter."

"Oh dear! It's all right! Sir, it's like you've seen it with your own eyes. Really, a threatening letter came last month. I don't know what he's offended in his fortune that it would turn out like this."

"There is a Xuanwu thief star in his fortune. This constellation is very powerful. If it's really offended, even his life will be in danger. You must think of a way to resolve it as soon as possible to avoid disaster."

"Sir, what is the way to resolve it?"

"Easy, easy. Just do a day of merit to resolve this evil constellation, and you can eliminate disasters and add blessings. We have Taoists here who specialize in doing merit on behalf of guests."

"Then how much money does it cost to do a day of merit?"

"It's limited, not much. We're newly opened, so we're just trying to make a name for ourselves. It only costs forty yuan."

"The money is up to you at forty yuan, but the work must be done properly," Mrs. Li said. She took out a ten-yuan banknote from the small wallet she was carrying and threw it on the table, saying, "This is a deposit of ten yuan. Sir, please accept it. I'll pay the rest after the matter is completed satisfactorily." After saying that, she got up and walked out.

"Don't be polite. Madam, please sit for a while. Excuse us for not seeing you off," the blind man said, standing up by the table. "Really talking nonsense. If I asked you to see me off, you wouldn't be able to," the rickshaw puller A San said with a grin outside the door.

Learning to Write

The Three People You Admire Most

— Old Tang

Last year, as the summer vacation was approaching, the school exams had already finished. We had packed our bedding, ready to attend the graduation ceremony and then head home to enjoy our lovely, sweet, once-a-year summer vacation.

Suddenly, a notice appeared on the "bulletin board," summoning our graduating class to assemble in the classroom. The teacher arrived, bringing a stack of forms, saying they were to be filled out by us at the request of the Municipal Education Bureau.

Among the questions on the form was this one: "The three people you admire most." Following these words were three horizontal lines, for us to fill in three names.

So, those who admired political leaders filled in Washington, Briand, and Wang Jingwei. Those who liked science wrote Edison, Newton, and Einstein. Those who had always been domineering at school filled in Napoleon, Chiang Kai-shek, and Feng Yuxiang.

Suddenly, a classmate stood up and asked, "Teacher, can we fill in Shanghai celebrities ××…××……××?"

Before the teacher could answer, the entire class burst into laughter.

Movies

### Road Hero

Charlie Chaplin's "Road Hero," starring the king of comedy, premiered yesterday at the Paris Grand Theatre. It was sold out before two o'clock, because this film is Chaplin's ten-year masterpiece and one of the three great works he considers most satisfying. Moreover, since Chaplin is not coming to China for the time being, watching this film is like quenching one's thirst by looking at plums. The story is as follows: Charlie is a homeless wanderer who follows a group of immigrants from Europe to America, preparing to start a new life. On the ship with him is a widow and her daughter. Charlie becomes very good friends with both of them. Somehow, on the ship, the widow has all her money stolen. Charlie finds out and feels very sorry for her, so he gives her all the money he won from gambling. When Charlie arrives in America, he has no money and wants to find something to do. His stomach is rumbling with hunger, and he walks alone on the street. Unconsciously, he walks into a restaurant and suddenly meets the girl who was on the ship with him. He has to treat her to something to eat, but he only has a dollar that he just picked up from the ground. Fortunately, he meets an artist who commissions Charlie and the girl to do some work. He is very happy, but soon he is unemployed again. Because he can't afford the rent, he has to go to jail. Taking advantage of the guards' inattention, he escapes. The guards chase him from behind, but Charlie uses special methods to avoid being caught. He escapes to another city and wants to change his life, so he becomes a policeman. But there is a local bully who is rampant and feared by everyone. When Charlie takes office, he sees the bully's ferocious appearance and cannot help but feel afraid. But he is brave after all. He thinks, "Either I don't do this job, or if I do, I must defeat this bully." Charlie makes up his mind. He uses a particularly clever method to finally subdue the bully. At this time, we can see Charlie happily walking with his girlfriend on the quiet streets of the city.

### Love Habit

"Love Habit," which premiered today at the Carlton, is not only funny but also romantic. Briefly, a husband has an affair, and another lecherous man takes the opportunity to seduce his wife. The entertainment subtly implies a warning, which is a wake-up call for wayward husbands. The protagonist, Seymour Hicks, is not only a famous stage performer but also a very famous playwright. He has traveled all over the world and has a thorough understanding of human psychology. He wrote the script himself and played the main role. All the other actors were also carefully selected by him, resulting in this excellent achievement, which is no accident. Anyone who wants to see a good film should not miss it.

### Possessed

The great star Joan Crawford's latest film "Possessed" is now showing at the Cathay Theatre on Avenue Joffre. Briefly, a young woman from a humble family initially uses her body to seek wealth and status, and then abandons wealth and status to show true love. Not only is the plot sad and beautiful, but the performance is also extraordinarily outstanding. It is indeed Joan Crawford's unprecedented work. Her co-star, Clark Gable, has always been praised as a handsome man, and his performance in this film is also profound and moving.

Jiangsu High Court Third Branch

Criminal Judgment One case of Pan Xiaosi causing death by negligence in business and an attached civil suit, the first trial was appealed. This court's ruling is as follows (Main text) The original judgment regarding the criminal part is revoked. Pan Xiaosi caused death by negligence in business and is sentenced to six months of imprisonment. Pre-trial detention days are counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. The attached civil appeal is rejected. One case of Gu Bainan appealing a first instance judgment of the Jiangsu Shanghai Second Special District Court for theft. This court's ruling is as follows (Main text) The appeal is rejected. (May 17)

Shanghai First Special District Court

Criminal First Instance Judgments ▲ New Gate Police Station sues Wang Caiqing for suspicion of theft (Main text) Wang Caiqing is not guilty. ▲ Huishan Police Station sues Zhang Shunxing for theft (Main text) Zhang Shunxing, a recidivist, is sentenced to ten months of imprisonment for theft. The stolen goods are to be returned to the owner according to the list. ▲ Old Gate Police Station sues Wu Tinghe for theft (Main text) Wu Tinghe, a recidivist, is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for theft. A one-foot ruler is to be returned to the owner. ▲ Huisi Police Station sues Zhong Zhaoen et al. for opium smoking (Main text) Zhong Zhu, Zhou Zou, and Zhong Zhaoen and Shi Xiangyu are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment for smoking and helping others to smoke opium. The smoking paraphernalia is confiscated according to the list. ▲ Jing'an Temple Police Station sues Wang Mingqi et al. for theft (Main text) Wang Mingqi and Yu Longsheng, recidivists, are each sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for theft. ▲ New Gate Police Station sues Liu Zhangzhi for theft (Main text) Liu Zhangzhi is sentenced to thirty days of detention for theft. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Yang Si et al. for theft (Main text) Yang Si and Yang Ziyang are each sentenced to two months of imprisonment for jointly committing theft. Two salted fish are to be returned to the owner. ▲ General Police Station sues Song Chunshan et al. for obstructing freedom (Main text) Song Chunshan and Cao Ronggen are each sentenced to six months of imprisonment for jointly illegally searching another person's body. ▲ General Police Station sues Chen Axiang for theft (Main text) Chen Axiang, a recidivist, is sentenced to ten months of imprisonment for theft. Ten iron bars are to be returned to the original owner. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Zhu Jiang for possession of opium (Main text) Zhu Jiang is fined thirty yuan for the crime of possessing opium. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The original package of opium is confiscated. Hongkou Police Station sues Wang Yan for possession of opium (Main text) Wang Yan is fined twenty yuan for the crime of possessing opium. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The original package of opium is confiscated. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Chen Akang, Wang Afu, et al. for gambling (Main text) Chen Akang, Wang Fusheng, Xu Asan, Zhou Shuimao, Ye Changfa, Pan Axiang, Ying Xingsheng, Chen Yongyue, Jiang Xinfa, Bian Fugui, Qiu Genrui, and Chen Yinchun are each fined four yuan for the crime of jointly gambling. If the fine is not paid by compulsory execution, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Gambling paraphernalia and gambling money are confiscated. ▲ Putuo Road Police Station sues Liu Zuode et al. for assault (Main text) Liu Zuode, Zhou Asi, Yu Hongfu, Xia Bingkun, Xia Yuying, and Xia Cui are each fined twenty yuan for the crime of jointly assaulting another person. If the fine is not paid by compulsory execution, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Chen Caizhi is not guilty. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Shen Lu et al. for gambling (Main text) Shen Lu is sentenced to one month of imprisonment for gathering people to gamble. Jiang Zhanglin, Lu Er, Yu Quanzhong, Zhou Age, Xia Qingfu, Gao Lianchu, Jiang Lianfa, Jiang Xianshou, and Zhang Hongsheng are each fined four yuan for the crime of jointly gambling. If the fine is not paid by compulsory execution, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Gambling paraphernalia and gambling money are confiscated. ▲ Huisi Police Station sues Luo Tuozi for opium (Main text) Luo Tuozi is fined sixty yuan for the crime of possessing opium. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The opium paraphernalia is confiscated. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Li Changying for bribery (Main text) Li Changying is fined ten yuan for the crime of violating police regulations. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The crime of offering a bribe is reduced to one month of imprisonment. The bribe money is confiscated. ▲ New Gate Police Station sues Wang Agen for theft (Main text) Wang Agen is sentenced to four months of imprisonment for the crime of theft. ▲ Huisi Police Station sues Li Agen et al. for opium (Main text) Li Agen is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of smoking opium. The smoking paraphernalia is confiscated. ▲ Huixi Police Station sues Yu Lin et al. for assault (Main text) Wang Linzhi is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for assault. Tong Liming is fined twenty yuan for assault. Zhang Xingde is fined thirty yuan for assault. Zhang Hangsheng and two others are each fined ten yuan for assault. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. ▲ Yangshupu Police Station sues Ma Longren for theft (Main text) Ma Longren is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of theft. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Xu Xiaodi for opium (Main text) Xu Xiaodi is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of smoking opium and fined thirty yuan. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The opium and smoking paraphernalia are confiscated. ▲ Huisi Police Station sues Wang Heshang et al. for opium (Main text) Wang Heshang is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for the crime of smoking opium. Xue Qu is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for providing opium to others and fined thirty yuan. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The smoking paraphernalia is confiscated. ▲ Jiaxing Road Police Station sues Lu Weibin for theft (Main text) Lu Weibin is sentenced to five months of imprisonment for the crime of theft. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Silas Da Kaufer Sigan for assault (Main text) Silas Da Kaufer Sigan is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for the crime of assaulting a senior relative. ▲ Jiaxing Road Police Station sues Zhang Qi et al. for opium (Main text) Zhang Qi is sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined fifty yuan for intending to profit by providing premises for others to smoke opium. If the fine is not paid, imprisonment for a certain term will be calculated as one day. Wang Bao, Shen Genlin, and Min Ajin, recidivists, are each sentenced to two months of imprisonment for smoking opium. Han Zhengyong and Min Agen are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment for smoking opium. Pre-trial detention days are counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. Opium smoking paraphernalia, etc. are confiscated. Qi Qi is not guilty. ▲ Gordon Road Police Station sues Tan Xiuqiao for theft (Main text) Tan Xiuqiao is sentenced to three years and six months of imprisonment for theft, violent resistance at the scene, and recidivism. Pre-trial detention days are counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲ General Police Station sues Xia Meiqi for theft (Main text) Xia Meiqi is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for theft. Pre-trial detention days are counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲ Old Gate Police Station sues Zhang Asheng for robbery (Main text) Zhang Asheng, a recidivist, is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for robbery. Pre-trial detention days are counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲ Old Gate Police Station sues Fu Agen et al. for extortion (Main text) Fu Agen is sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for each of seven counts of extortion, with a total of two years of imprisonment. Pre-trial detention days are counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. Yao Fusheng is sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for each of three counts of extortion, with a total of one year of imprisonment. Pre-trial detention days are counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Pan Chen for possession of opium (Main text) Pan Chen is fined forty yuan for the crime of possessing opium. The stolen goods are to be returned to the owner. ▲ Yangshupu Police Station sues Su Jinsheng for robbery (Main text) Su Jinsheng, armed and in a gang, is sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for each of three counts of robbery, for a total of nine years of imprisonment. Pre-trial detention days are counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. ▲ Hongkou Police Station sues Li San et al. for opium (Main text) Li San is sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined one hundred yuan for intending to profit by providing premises for others to smoke opium. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every yuan. If the fine is not paid, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Notice of Auction This court is executing a case in which the creditor Shui Lai Sheng and the debtor Shen Guisheng, et al. are involved in a dispute over a loan. The debtor Yao Adu's real estate described below has been sealed and appraised, with a minimum price set. Bidding will be held at the court entrance on May 17, and the bidding will close on May 31 with number nine as the bidding number. Residents who wish to purchase this real estate should submit a sealed letter with their name, age, place of origin, address, occupation, and the price they are willing to pay. The court will open the bids on the specified date and award the property to the highest bidder. The successful bidder must pay one-fifth of the bid price as a deposit immediately and pay the remaining balance in one lump sum upon delivery of the property, at which time the court will issue a title deed. If the bidder fails to pay within the deadline, the property will be awarded to the next highest bidder, following the same procedure. All residents should be aware of this notice, and all interested parties should be present on the opening date to avoid any misunderstandings. This notice is hereby issued. (Details are as follows) (1) Object of the auction: a house with a lane land of five li (2) Location of the property: Jiangjia Lane, Gordon Road (3) Minimum price: 439 silver dollars (4) Location for viewing the records: the office of the court clerk (5) Persons to contact for viewing: Shui Laisheng and Wang Zhixiang, court clerk (6) Any claims of right to the real estate must be declared to the court within seven days of this notice.

Notice of Auction This court is executing a case in which the creditor Pan Zhengquan and the debtor Ye Jinsheng are involved in a dispute over a mortgage loan. The debtor's real estate described below has been sealed and appraised, with a minimum price set. Bidding will be held at the court entrance on May 17, and the bidding will close on May 31 with number eight as the bidding number. Residents who wish to purchase this real estate should submit a sealed letter with their name, age, place of origin, address, occupation, and the price they are willing to pay. The court will open the bids on the specified date and award the property to the highest bidder. The successful bidder must pay one-fifth of the bid price as a deposit immediately and pay the remaining balance in one lump sum upon delivery of the property, at which time the court will issue a title deed. If the bidder fails to pay within the deadline, the property will be awarded to the next highest bidder, following the same procedure. All residents should be aware of this notice, and all interested parties should be present on the opening date to avoid any misunderstandings. This notice is hereby issued. (Details are as follows) (1) Object of the auction: Two fen three li three hao of arable land along with two lean-to houses. (2) Location of the property: No. 8, Dezi Xu, twelfth tu, twenty-seventh bao north (3) Minimum price: 1245.75 silver dollars (4) Location for viewing the records: the office of the court clerk (5) Persons to contact for viewing: Pan Zhengquan and Ying Sheng San, court clerk (6) Any claims of right to the real estate must be declared to the court within seven days of this notice (May 17).

Shanghai Second Special District Local Court

Criminal Judgments

Police Department vs. Zhang Mingxi Opium Case (Main Text): Zhang Mingxi is fined ten yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. One opium pipe, one opium lamp, one opium needle, and one opium tray are all confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Qian Maotou Opium Case (Main Text): Qian Maotou is fined forty yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. One opium pipe, one opium lamp, and two opium needles are all confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Yao Debiao Opium Case (Main Text): Yao Debiao is fined seventy yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. One opium pipe, one opium lamp, one opium needle, one opium knife, and one opium tray are all confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Pan Xingrong Opium Case (Main Text): Pan Xingrong is fined sixty yuan for possessing opium. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. Two small boxes of opium paste are all confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Ma Chen Stealing Case (Main Text): Ma Chen is sentenced to fifteen days of detention for theft. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of detention for every two days.

Police Department vs. Chen Ansheng Stealing Case (Main Text): Chen Ansheng is sentenced to fifty days of detention for theft. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of detention for every two days.

Police Department vs. Wang Ayou Stealing Case (Main Text): Wang Ayou is sentenced to thirty days of detention for theft. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of detention for every two days.

Police Department vs. Wang Jiali Stealing Case (Main Text): Wang Jiali, a repeat offender, is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for theft. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Police Department vs. Li Wenkui Stealing Case (Main Text): Li Wenkui is sentenced to ten days of detention for theft. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of detention for every two days.

Police Department vs. Cai Rongquan Opium Case (Main Text): Cai Rongquan is fined forty yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. One opium pipe, one opium lamp, one opium needle, and one opium tray are all confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Zhang Xiuying Opium Case (Main Text): Zhang Xiuying is fined forty yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. Opium lamp and other items listed are confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Kong Mingjie Opium Case (Main Text): Kong Mingjie is fined forty yuan for possessing opium and opium paraphernalia. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. Two opium pipes, one opium lamp, one opium tray, five opium bubbles, and half a jar of opium ash are all confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Lu Heshang Opium Case (Main Text): Lu Heshang is fined eighty yuan for possessing opium. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. Eight small boxes of opium paste are all confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Liu Zude et al. Opium Case (Main Text): Liu Zude is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for providing a place for others to smoke opium substitutes. Zhu Bin is sentenced to one month of imprisonment for smoking opium substitutes. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of imprisonment for every two days. Three opium pipes and opium trays, etc., are all confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Xu Hongsheng et al. Opium Case (Main Text): Xu Hongsheng is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for providing a place for others to smoke opium substitutes. Zhang Zifang and Jin Shaozhang are sentenced to one month in jail for smoking opium substitutes. Three opium pipes and five red pills are confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Zhang Baoqi Injury Case (Main Text): Zhang Baoqi is found not guilty.

Police Department vs. Zhou Changfu Gambling Case (Main Text): Zhou Changfu is fined two hundred yuan for the crime of gambling. If unable to pay, one day of imprisonment will be substituted for every two yuan. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of two yuan of the fine for each day. Gambling dice and gambling tools as listed are confiscated.

Police Department vs. Lu Jisheng Stealing Case (Main Text): Lu Jisheng is sentenced to twenty days of detention for theft. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of detention for every two days. Sentence suspended for two years.

Police Department vs. Yao Li et al. Opium Case (Main Text): Yao Li is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for providing a place for others to smoke opium substitutes. Yao Shunhou is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for assisting in providing a place for others to smoke opium substitutes. Tang Ping is sentenced to one month of imprisonment for smoking opium substitutes. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Plaintiff Meng Xijiu vs. Li Dongjiao Embezzlement Case (Main Text): This case is not accepted.

Police Department vs. Wang Zhiwen et al. Stolen Goods Case (Main Text): Wang Zhiwen, Xu Changsheng, and Zhang Sibao are all found not guilty.

Police Department vs. Sun Fengshan Stealing Case (Main Text): Sun Fengshan is sentenced to forty days of detention for theft. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of detention for every two days.

Police Department vs. Liu Amao et al. Opium Case (Main Text): Liu Amao is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for providing a place for others to smoke opium substitutes. Mei Jiahong is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for assisting in providing a place for others to smoke opium substitutes. Zhang Shunyuan, Chen Shaoting, Zhao Aquan, Wang Aliu, and Liu Fengshan are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment for smoking opium substitutes. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of imprisonment for every two days. Zhang Shunyuan and Liu Fengshan each receive a suspended sentence of two years. Five opium pipes and twenty red pills as listed are confiscated and destroyed.

Police Department vs. Chen Asi et al. Gambling Case (Main Text): Chen Asi is sentenced to two months of imprisonment and fined one hundred yuan for providing a gambling venue for profit. Days of detention before the judgment is final will be credited at a rate of one day of imprisonment for every two days. Police Department vs. Zhao Atao et al. Opium Case (Main Text): Zhao Atao is sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined one hundred yuan for the crime of providing a place for others to smoke opium for profit.
